< text>
Just went to try Double Shot Cafe on 4587 Mission. They have very friendly staff. I am disappointed with their quality and selection of their product though. While I was waiting for my beverage I spotted mold on their banana bread that's kept right next to unpacked cookies. I let the staff know. At first they tried to explain away the mold by saying that it was "the organic stuff."  She's correct that mold is organic. I had to physically point it out the moldy corners to the at lady at the register. She then delegated for her colleague to take away the banana cakes. The co-worker said she didn't see anything wrong with them and I again had to show her the corners of the banana cakes. They took away the banana bread but still kept the unpacked cookies that were near the mold in stock.
I was in for a second disappointment when I received my beverage finally. I got an Horchata Latte Frappuccino. It was a super super sweet, greasy and absurdly chunky ice mess. There were huge chunks of ice that got stuck in the straw right away. The super saccharine greasy drink was a huge disappointment for the $4.25. After the first few gross sips I threw it away fearing the worse since such a new business is already selling moldy food.< /text>

This is a hip little coffee shop amongst a bustling street of other retail businesses. But inside you can cozy up with a hot cup of tea (or my favorite, the prepackaged extra large carton of coconut water) and play some board games. Jenga is extra fun because it's generally quiet so if you lose and make it fall, you feel more self-conscious. More incentive to win! If you win or lose, I recommend the apple tart pastry. If you're okay walking a bit, I've trekked from Glen Park BART through the neighborhood; you pass by some cool views over the hills too.< /text>

<Pics>None<//Pics><Resp>None< /Resp><Review>Food was good, servers were friendly.  Slightly slow.< /Review></record></dataset><record>
<Time>1569713856168</Time>< Text>
Always tough to fairly rate a brand new business/restaurant. Will update as additional visits occur.

The good - the location, vibe, and layout are great. They really did a nice job the overall design and artwork.  The Korean Pepper Wings and seasoned wedge fries were really good. I found the Pesto/Garlic Wings were flat on flavor. The wait staff seemed a little inexperienced but were very friendly and attentive, I'm sure they will get even better as time goes on.

The bad - no drink menus when we went. It took  a long time to get the place open, it seems like there was plenty of time to get this done prior to opening.  Given the sports bar vibe (lots of tv's and wait staff in jerseys) you would think they would have some kind of happy hour or game day specials. There is a beautiful full bar so a shame not to have it better promoted.

The ugly - $10 for a glass of house Cabernet Sauvignon and $9 IPA are way overpriced. You are in Lodi wine country, a glass of house wine would generally be under $10 and beer $5 - $6.

Will I be back? Sure, I like supporting local businesses. Probably will stick with water, no need for two drinks to be half the bill.</Text>

<Rating>1< /Rating><text>Incredibly disappointing overall. It was my first time here today, but this place has a long line of people waiting as soon as it opens and is highly reviewed, so I thought it would be a pretty solid place to get a cut. I was able to get in right as they opened and had my hair cut by an older gentleman whose name I unfortunately didn't get.

I showed a photo of the cut that I wanted - short sides with a slight fade, long on top with hair parted to the side and back, as well as a beard trim. It's a pretty standard cut and the photo was good enough so that no other barber ever had an issue getting it right. My barber glanced at it and assured me that he would take care of me...

The actual cut turned out to be nothing like the photo or what I wanted. There's no fade to speak of; the sides and back are pretty much buzzed. The hair in front is long, but gets extremely short at the back and at the top of the head, which is nothing like what I wanted... On top of that, the $15 beard trim was a 2-minute job and the barber didn't even touch the whiskers. I also asked him to keep the beard at the same length and he did - with the exception of my cheeks, where he shaved everything off. I don't understand why.

I'm sure there's a decent amount of technical skill here, but my barber made no effort to understand what I wanted exactly. He didn't ask me any questions about what I wanted during the cut - he made up his mind based on that one glance at the photo and he thought he knew what I wanted. This isn't how a GOOD barbershop operates. Lack of attention to detail during the beard trim is just icing on this crappy cake. And yeah, I wish I said something or complained after it was all done but there was no point - can't make hair longer after the fact.

In short, this was incredibly, incredibly disappointing. I don't get the feeling these folks know much besides doing a few very basic, common hairstyles. I don't get the feeling they care. Like I said it was my first time but based on my experience today I won't be back, and I'd never recommend this place to anyone.

Please see my photos for the beard trim and judge the quality for yourself.

Checked out other reviews on Yelp and saw two other one star reviews for a barber named Oscar, furthest station from the window... Their experience matches mine exactly and I'm sure this was my barber as well. According to them the barber didn't listen and cut their hair much too short, leaving them with an awful cut. Once again, please beware if you do come to this shop... or rather, don't come at all. How or why this is allowed after multiple people complained about this thing is baffling... and think about how many just walked away unhappy without leaving a review.< /text>< pictures>
